## H. ROP / Redundancy Analysis

The benchmark does not label a knee point. For this report, the diagnostic knee point is inferred per algorithm/seed as the feasible entry with the largest sum `MSR + CGCC + ETR`. ROP is diagnostic only and is not an optimization objective.

Lower ROP means less duplicate coverage among selected tests. Because most Lang 5b rows are empty, selected_count and ETR are especially important for interpretation: an algorithm can select many empty tests without improving coverage, which lowers ETR without improving MSR or CGCC.

## I. Statistical Analysis

| Comparison | Wilcoxon p-value | AR wins | AR losses | Ties | Interpretation |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| ar_qiea > mo_qiea | 0.000000596046 | 25 | 5 | 0 | AR-QIEA significantly greater |
| ar_qiea > nsga2 | 0.999999004416 | 5 | 25 | 0 | Not evidence that AR-QIEA is greater |
| ar_qiea > random_front | 0.999999764375 | 3 | 27 | 0 | Not evidence that AR-QIEA is greater |

P1 gate result: `FAIL`.

Mean HV AR-QIEA = 0.534611; MO-QIEA = 0.529235; random_front = 0.577086. The SPEC gate requires AR-QIEA to have HV at least MO-QIEA and random_front, preferably with p < 0.05. Lang 5b fails this gate because AR-QIEA is below NSGA-II and random_front on mean HV, and the one-sided Wilcoxon tests versus those baselines do not support AR-QIEA superiority.

## J. Detailed Interpretation

- Best HV mean: `random_front` with mean HV 0.577086.
- Largest mean Pareto front: `mo_qiea` with mean front size 15.366667.
- Best mean MSR: `ar_qiea`.
- Best mean CGCC: `ar_qiea`.
- Best mean ETR: `random_front`.
- Runtime trade-off: `random_front` is fastest by mean runtime; among search algorithms, compare section D. The full run completed in approximately 82.34 minutes.
- Paper-claim support: `FAIL` for Lang 5b. This run does not support the claim that AR-QIEA has higher HV than MO-QIEA and random_front with statistical confidence.
- Dataset limitation: Lang 5b is internally consistent but sparse in a degenerate way: 2217 of 2230 tests have zero coverage in the matrix. This makes ETR and selected_count behavior dominate much of the practical interpretation.
- Synthetic risk limitation: MSR, CGCC, and execution times are P1 synthetic/proxy values generated from coverage and risk_seed=12345, not real Major mutation or real call-graph centrality.

```powershell
..\.venv\Scripts\python.exe -c "import csv,json; from pathlib import Path; p=Path('datasets/defects4j/Lang/5b'); tests=[x.strip() for x in (p/'tests.txt').read_text(encoding='utf-8-sig').splitlines() if x.strip()]; reqs=[x.strip() for x in (p/'requirements.txt').read_text(encoding='utf-8-sig').splitlines() if x.strip()]; rows=list(csv.reader((p/'matrix.csv').open(newline='',encoding='utf-8-sig'))); header,data=rows[0],rows[1:]; meta=json.loads((p/'metadata.json').read_text(encoding='utf-8-sig')); print({'tests':len(tests),'requirements':len(reqs),'matrix_shape':(len(data),len(header)-1),'covered_requirements':sum(any(r[j+1].strip() in {'1','true','t'} for r in data) for j in range(len(reqs))),'empty_tests':sum(not any(c.strip() in {'1','true','t'} for c in r[1:]) for r in data),'duplicate_tests':len(tests)-len(set(tests)),'duplicate_requirements':len(reqs)-len(set(reqs)),'tests_match':tests==[r[0] for r in data],'requirements_match':reqs==header[1:],'metadata':meta})"
```
